House File 2224 - Introduced


                                 HOUSE FILE 

                                 HOUSE FILE 
                                 HOUSE FILE                                  HOUSE FILE                                  BY  HEDDENS

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists,
  2    making penalties applicable, providing for fees, and
  3    including effective date and implementation provisions.
  4 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 5481HH (4) 86
    tr/nh

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.  Section 135.24, subsection 7, paragraph d, Code
  1  2 2016, is amended to read as follows:
  1  3    d.  "Health care provider" means a physician licensed under
  1  4 chapter 148, a chiropractor licensed under chapter 151, a
  1  5 physical therapist licensed pursuant to chapter 148A, an
  1  6 occupational therapist licensed pursuant to chapter 148B,
  1  7 a podiatrist licensed pursuant to chapter 149, a physician
  1  8 assistant licensed and practicing under a supervising physician
  1  9 pursuant to chapter 148C, a licensed practical nurse, a
  1 10 registered nurse, or an advanced registered nurse practitioner
  1 11 licensed pursuant to chapter 152 or 152E, a respiratory
  1 12 therapist licensed pursuant to chapter 152B, a dentist, dental
  1 13 hygienist, or dental assistant registered or licensed to
  1 14 practice under chapter 153, an optometrist licensed pursuant to
  1 15 chapter 154, a psychologist licensed pursuant to chapter 154B,
  1 16 a social worker licensed pursuant to chapter 154C, a mental
  1 17 health counselor

  6 24    Sec. 13.    6 24    Sec. 13.    6 25 therapy.
  6 26    1.  An applicant for a license to practice clinical art
  6 27 therapy shall be granted a license by the board when the
  6 28 applicant satisfies all of the following requirements:
  6 29    a.  Possesses a master's or doctoral degree from a nationally
  6 30 accredited institution consisting of at least sixty semester
  6 31 hours, or its equivalent, in an art therapy program approved
  6 32 by the American art therapy association or its successor, or a
  6 33 substantially equivalent program as approved by the board.
  6 34    b.  Has at least two years of supervised experience or its
  6 35 equivalent as approved by the board that includes experience
  7  1 in a clinical setting that provides opportunities to diagnose,
  7  2 treat, appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  7  3 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  7  4 determined by the board by rule. Standards for supervision,
  7  5 including the requirement that supervision be provided by
  7  6 an art therapy certified supervisor credentialed by the art
  7  7 therapy credentials board or other qualified licensed mental
  7  8 health professional approved by the board, shall be determined
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.

  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  6 28 applicant satisfies all of the following requirements:
  6 29    a.  Possesses a master's or doctoral degree from a nationally
  6 30 accredited institution consisting of at least sixty semester
  6 31 hours, or its equivalent, in an art therapy program approved
  6 32 by the American art therapy association or its successor, or a
  6 33 substantially equivalent program as approved by the board.
  6 34    b.  Has at least two years of supervised experience or its
  6 35 equivalent as approved by the board that includes experience
  7  1 in a clinical setting that provides opportunities to diagnose,
  7  2 treat, appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  7  3 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  7  4 determined by the board by rule. Standards for supervision,
  7  5 including the requirement that supervision be provided by
  7  6 an art therapy certified supervisor credentialed by the art
  7  7 therapy credentials board or other qualified licensed mental
  7  8 health professional approved by the board, shall be determined
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  6 33 substantially equivalent program as approved by the board.
  6 34    b.  Has at least two years of supervised experience or its
  6 35 equivalent as approved by the board that includes experience
  7  1 in a clinical setting that provides opportunities to diagnose,
  7  2 treat, appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  7  3 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  7  4 determined by the board by rule. Standards for supervision,
  7  5 including the requirement that supervision be provided by
  7  6 an art therapy certified supervisor credentialed by the art
  7  7 therapy credentials board or other qualified licensed mental
  7  8 health professional approved by the board, shall be determined
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7  3 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  7  4 determined by the board by rule. Standards for supervision,
  7  5 including the requirement that supervision be provided by
  7  6 an art therapy certified supervisor credentialed by the art
  7  7 therapy credentials board or other qualified licensed mental
  7  8 health professional approved by the board, shall be determined
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7  8 health professional approved by the board, shall be determined
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7  9 by the board by rule.
  7 10    c.  Passes the national board examination of the art therapy
  7 11 credentials board or its successor.
  7 12    2.  The board may make a determination that a program is
  7 13 substantially equivalent to a master's degree program in art
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.

  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7 14 therapy approved by the American art therapy association or its
  7 15 successor if the program includes an art therapy internship
  7 16 of not less than six hundred hours that is performed under
  7 17 supervision and is part of an approved course of study and
  7 18 graduate=level courses and training in the following areas:
  7 19    a.  The art therapy profession.
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7 20    b.  Theory and practice of art therapy.
  7 21    c.  Human growth and developmental dynamics in art.
  7 22    d.  Application of art therapy with people in different
  7 23 treatment settings.
  7 24    e.  Art therapy appraisal, diagnosis, and assessment.
  7 25    f.  Ethical and legal issues of art therapy practice.
  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  7 26    g.  Matters of cultural and social diversity bearing on the
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.
  7 30    Sec. 14.  TRANSITION PROVISIONS.
  7 31    1.  Notwithstanding sections 147.14, as amended in this
  7 32 Act, and 147.16, the governor may appoint, as the initial
  7 33 member licensed to practice clinical art therapy to the board
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7 27 practice of art therapy.
  7 28    h.  Standards of good art therapy practice.
  7 29    i.  Group art therapy.

  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  7 34 of behavioral science pursuant to section 147.14, subsection
  7 35 1, paragraph "m", as amended in this Act, an individual who
  8  1 is credentialed as a board=certified art therapist by the
  8  2 art therapy credentials board with experience and expertise
  8  3 substantially equivalent to the requirements for licensure as a
  8  4 clinical art therapist under section 154D.8, as enacted in this
  8  5 Act.
  8  6    2.  Notwithstanding section 154D.8, subsection 1, as
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act

  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  8  7 enacted in this Act, during the period of one year from the
  8  8 effective date of rules implementing this Act, the board
  8  9 may grant a license to practice clinical art therapy for an
  8 10 applicant who provides documentation satisfactory to the board
  8 11 that the applicant holds a credential in good standing as a
  8 12 board=certified art therapist with the art therapy credentials
  8 13 board and has been engaged in the practice of clinical art
  8 14 therapy for not less than five years at the time of the
  8 15 effective date of rules adopted by the board to implement this
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.

  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  8 16 Act, which shall include experience in a clinical setting
  8 17 that provides substantial opportunities to diagnose, treat,
  8 18 appraise, and assess mental, emotional, behavioral, and
  8 19 addiction disorders in both individual and group settings, as
  8 20 determined by the board by rule.
  8 21    Sec. 15.  EFFECTIVE DATE AND IMPLEMENTATION.  This Act
  8 22 shall take effect January 1, 2017, except that the board of
  8 23 behavioral science may begin implementation prior to that date,
  8 24 to the extent necessary to fully implement the provisions
  8 25 providing for the licensure of clinical art therapists by
  8 26 January 1, 2017.
  8 27                           EXPLANATION
  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary

  8 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 30    This bill provides for the licensure of clinical art
  8 31 therapists. Under the bill, the board of behavioral science
  8 32 shall administer the licensure of clinical art therapists and
  8 33 shall adopt rules relating to the practice of clinical art
  8 34 therapy. The bill modifies the membership of the board of
  8 35 behavioral science to add one clinical art therapist and remove
  9  1 one public member. The bill provides that persons not licensed
  9  2 under the bill but referring to themselves as clinical art
  9  3 therapists or using other similar terms or abbreviations shall
  9  4 be guilty of a simple misdemeanor. A simple misdemeanor is
  9  5 punishable by confinement for no more than 30 days or a fine of
  9  6 at least $65 but not more than $625 or by both.
  9  7    The bill defines several terms including "art therapy"
  9  8 and "clinical art therapy". The bill provides for temporary
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh

  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5481HH (4) 86
       tr/nh
  9  9 licensure of clinical art therapists and sets forth standards
  9 10 for continuing education requirements for licensed clinical
  9 11 art therapists. The bill requires that to acquire a license
  9 12 to practice art therapy, an applicant must have a master's or
  9 13 doctoral degree in art therapy from a program approved by the
  9 14 American art therapy association or another program approved
  9 15 by the board of behavioral science, pass a national board
  9 16 examination, and complete at least two years of supervised
  9 17 experience.
  9 18    The bill includes licensed certified art therapists as
  9 19 "health care providers" eligible to provide services through
  9 20 the volunteer health care provider program created in Code
  9 21 section 135.24. The bill provides that the board of behavioral
  9 22 science may waive the licensing requirements established by
  9 23 the bill for persons with certain qualifications in the first
  9 24 year after rules implementing the licensure of clinical art
  9 25 therapists are adopted. The bill includes an effective date of
  9 26 January 1, 2017, except that the board of behavioral science
  9 27 may begin implementation prior to that date, to the extent
  9 28 necessary to fully implement the provisions providing for the
  9 29 licensure of clinical art therapists by January 1, 2017.
